
### PHP Yahoo OAuth 1.0a Authentication and API Access Example

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This comprehensive PHP example demonstrates the full OAuth 1.0a authentication flow for Yahoo APIs. It covers obtaining a request token, user authorization via a URL, capturing the verifier, exchanging for an access token, and then using that access token to make a sample API call. The script also includes logic to persist the access token data to a file for subsequent use, avoiding repeated authorization steps. Error handling for OAuth exceptions and API request failures is integrated.

```php
// 3. If none of that worked, send the user to get a new token
if( ! $access_token ) {

  print "Better try to get a new access token.\n";
  $o = new OAuth( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret,
                  OAUTH_SIG_METHOD_HMACSHA1, OAUTH_AUTH_TYPE_URI );
  $o->enableDebug();

  $request_token = NULL;

  try {
    $response = $o->getRequestToken( "https://api.login.yahoo.com/oauth/v2/get_request_token", 'oob' );
    $request_token = $response['oauth_token'];
    $request_secret = $response['oauth_token_secret'];

    print "Hey! Go to this URL and tell us the verifier you get at the end.\n";
    print ' ' . $response['xoauth_request_auth_url'] . "\n";

  } catch( OAuthException $e ) {
    print $e->getMessage() . "\n";
  }

  // Wait for input, then try to use it to get a new access token.
  if( $request_token && $request_secret ) {
    print "Type the verifier and hit enter...\n";
    $verifier = fgets( STDIN );
    $verifier = rtrim( $verifier );

    print "Here's the verifier you gave us: ${verifier}\n";

    try {
      $o->setToken( $request_token, $request_secret );
      $response = $o->getAccessToken( 'https://api.login.yahoo.com/oauth/v2/get_token', NULL, $verifier );

      print "Got it!\n";
      $access_token = $response['oauth_token'];
      $access_secret = $response['oauth_token_secret'];
      $access_session = $response['oauth_session_handle'];
      $store_access_token_data = true;
      print " Token: ${access_token}\n";
      print " Secret: ${access_secret}\n";
      print " Session Handle: ${access_session}\n\n";

    } catch( OAuthException $e ) {
      print 'Error: ' . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
      print 'Response: ' . $e->lastResponse . "\n";
      print "Shoot, couldn't get the access token. :(\n";
    }
  }

}

if( $access_token ) {

  // Try to make request using stored token
  try {
    $o->setToken( $access_token, $access_secret );
    if( $o->fetch( $url ) ) {
      print "Got data from API:\n\n";
      print $o->getLastResponse() . "\n\n";

      print "Successful!\n";
    } else {
      print "Couldn't fetch\n";
    }
  } catch( OAuthException $e ) {
    print 'Error: ' . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
    print 'Error Code: ' . $e->getCode() . "\n";
    print 'Response: ' . $e->lastResponse . "\n";
  }
}

// 4. Rewrite token information if necessary
if( $store_access_token_data ) {

  print "Looks like we need to store access token data! Doing that now.\n";

  $tok_fh = fopen( $token_file_name, 'w' );
  if( $tok_fh ) {
    fwrite( $tok_fh, "${access_token}\n" );
    fwrite( $tok_fh, "${access_secret}\n" );
    fwrite( $tok_fh, "${access_session}\n" );

    fclose( $tok_fh );
  } else {
    print "Hm, couldn't open file to write back access token information.\n";
  }
}
?>
```

### Users Collection URI Examples

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Illustrates various URI formats for extracting single or multiple sub-resources from the Users collection, including login and field-specific queries, demonstrating how to construct API requests.

```APIDOC
/users;use_login=1/{sub_resource}
/users;use_login=1;out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
/users;field={field_name1},{field_name2}
```

### Example XML for Yahoo Fantasy Sports Team Data

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This XML snippet provides a detailed structure for multiple fantasy sports teams, including their unique key, ID, name, associated URLs, team logos, division ID, FAAB balance, manager details (ID, nickname, GUID, commissioner status), season points, and comprehensive standings (rank, wins, losses, ties, percentage, divisional outcomes). Note that the first team's opening tag was inferred to complete the snippet.

```XML
<team>
          <name>Erickson - RotoWire</name>
          <url>https://football.fantasysports.yahoo.com/archive/pnfl/2009/431/13</url>
          <team_logos>
            <team_logo>
              <size>medium</size>
              <url>https://lookup.avatars.yahoo.com/images?yid=jeff_rotonews&amp;size=medium&amp;type=jpg&amp;pty=3000</url>
            </team_logo>
          </team_logos>
          <division_id>2</division_id>
          <faab_balance>17</faab_balance>
          <managers>
            <manager>
              <manager_id>11</manager_id>
              <nickname>-- hidden --</nickname>
              <guid>SB4Y5HVVUKMCTKZFQCXHIZ222E</guid>
            </manager>
          </managers>
          <team_points>
            <coverage_type>season</coverage_type>
            <season>2009</season>
            <total>1484.56</total>
          </team_points>
          <team_standings>
            <rank>9</rank>
            <outcome_totals>
              <wins>6</wins>
              <losses>7</losses>
              <ties>0</ties>
              <percentage>.462</percentage>
            </outcome_totals>
            <divisional_outcome_totals>
              <wins>3</wins>
              <losses>3</losses>
              <ties>0</ties>
            </divisional_outcome_totals>
          </team_standings>
        </team>
        <team>
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API: League Key Format

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Explains the specific format for league keys used in the API, providing examples and a crucial note about the separator character.

```APIDOC
.l.{league_id}

Example: pnfl.l.431 or 223.l.431

Note: The separator between the game_key and league_id is a lower case L (not the number 1).
```

### Complete Yahoo Fantasy Sports OAuth 1.0a Flow Example (PHP)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This is the main program demonstrating the entire OAuth 1.0a authentication and API interaction process. It orchestrates the calls to `get_request_token`, prompts the user for authorization by directing them to a URL, captures the verifier from standard input, calls `get_access_token`, and finally uses `make_request` to fetch data from the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. It includes basic error checking and command-line argument parsing for the API request URI.

```php
// **** MAIN PROGRAM STARTS HERE ****

$consumer_key = $consumer_data['test']['key'];
$consumer_secret = $consumer_data['test']['secret'];

// 1. Get Request Token
$request_token_data = get_request_token( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret );

if( ! $request_token_data ) {
  print "Could not retrieve request token data\n";
  exit;
}

$request_token = $request_token_data['oauth_token'];
$request_token_secret = $request_token_data['oauth_token_secret'];
$auth_url = $request_token_data['xoauth_request_auth_url'];

// 2. Direct user to Yahoo! for authorization (retrieve verifier)
print "Hey! Go to this URL and tell us the verifier you get at the end.\n";
print ' ' . $auth_url . "\n\n";

print "Type the verifier and hit enter...\n";
$verifier = fgets( STDIN );

print "Here's the verifier you gave us: ${verifier}\n";

// 3. Get Access Token
$access_token_data =
  get_access_token( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $request_token, $request_token_secret, $verifier );

if( ! $access_token_data ) {
  print "Could not get access token\n";
  exit;
}

$access_token = $access_token_data['oauth_token'];
$access_token_secret = $access_token_data['oauth_token_secret'];

// 4. Make request using Access Token
$base_url = 'https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/';
if( isset( $argv[1] ) ) {
  $request_uri = $argv[1];
} else {
  $request_uri = 'fantasy/v2/game/nfl';
}
$request_url = $base_url . $request_uri;

print "Making request for ${request_url}...\n";

$request_data = make_request( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $access_token, $access_token_secret, $request_url );

if( ! $request_data ) {
  print "Request failed\n";
}

$return_code = $request_data['return_code'];
$contents = $request_data['contents'];

print "Return code: ${return_code}\n";
print "Contents:\n${contents}\n\n";

print "Successful\n";

?>
```

### Complete Yahoo Fantasy Sports OAuth 1.0a Flow Example (PHP)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This is the main execution block demonstrating the full OAuth 1.0a authorization flow. It initializes consumer credentials, obtains a request token, prompts the user for authorization via a URL, captures the verifier, exchanges for an access token, and finally makes an authenticated call to the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API.

```php
$consumer_key = $consumer_data['test']['key'];
$consumer_secret = $consumer_data['test']['secret'];

// 1. Get Request Token
$request_token_data = get_request_token( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret );

if( ! $request_token_data ) {
  print "Could not retrieve request token data\n";
  exit;
}

$request_token = $request_token_data['oauth_token'];
$request_token_secret = $request_token_data['oauth_token_secret'];
$auth_url = $request_token_data['xoauth_request_auth_url'];

// 2. Direct user to Yahoo! for authorization (retrieve verifier)
print "Hey! Go to this URL and tell us the verifier you get at the end.\n";
print ' ' . $auth_url . "\n\n";

print "Type the verifier and hit enter...\n";
$verifier = fgets( STDIN );

print "Here's the verifier you gave us: ${verifier}\n";

// 3. Get Access Token
$access_token_data =
  get_access_token( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $request_token, $request_token_secret, $verifier );

if( ! $access_token_data ) {
  print "Could not get access token\n";
  exit;
}

$access_token = $access_token_data['oauth_token'];
$access_token_secret = $access_token_data['oauth_token_secret'];

// 4. Make request using Access Token
$base_url = 'https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/';
if( isset( $argv[1] ) ) {
  $request_uri = $argv[1];
} else {
  $request_uri = 'fantasy/v2/game/nfl';
}
$request_url = $base_url . $request_uri;

print "Making request for ${request_url}...\n";

$request_data = make_request( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $access_token, $access_token_secret, $request_url );

if( ! $request_data ) {
  print "Request failed\n";
}

$return_code = $request_data['return_code'];
$contents = $request_data['contents'];

print "Return code: ${return_code}\n";
print "Contents:\n${contents}\n\n";

print "Successful\n";

?>
```

### Using the 'out' Parameter for Extra Sub-Resources

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This URI example demonstrates the use of the 'out' parameter to fetch additional sub-resources (e.g., league settings) alongside a main resource chain. It shows how to retrieve specific league settings and two teams simultaneously, branching off the primary resource path.

```APIDOC
/fantasy/v2//;out=settings/;team_keys=,{team_key2}
```

### Implement OAuth 1.0a Signed Request and Response Parsing in PHP

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This PHP script demonstrates a complete OAuth 1.0a flow implementation from scratch. It includes a helper function `_make_signed_request` for generating signed GET requests with HMAC-SHA1 or PLAINTEXT signatures, handling parameter sorting, URL encoding, and cURL execution. Another helper function, `oauth_response_to_array`, is provided to parse OAuth response strings into an associative array. This example is useful for understanding the underlying mechanics of OAuth without relying on external libraries.

```php
<?php
// **** POTENTIAL CONFIGURATION STARTS HERE ****

// MODIFY: Insert your own consumer key and secret here!
$consumer_data = array();
$consumer_data['test']['key']    = '<INSERT CONSUMER KEY HERE>';
$consumer_data['test']['secret'] = '<INSERT CONSUMER SECRET HERE>';

// **** HELPER FUNCTIONS START HERE ****

///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//  FUNCTION _make_signed_request
/// @brief Helper function to make a signed OAuth request. Only allows GET
///        requests at the moment. Will add on standard OAuth params, but
///        you may need to fill in non-generic ones ahead of time.
///
/// @param[in]  $consumer_key      Application consumer key
/// @param[in]  $consumer_secret   Application consumer secret
/// @param[in]  $token             Token (request or access token)
/// @param[in]  $token_secret      Token secret
/// @param[in]  $signature_method  'PLAINTEXT' or 'HMAC-SHA1'
/// @param[in]  $url               URL to make request to
/// @param[in]  $params            Array of key=>val for params. Don't
///                                urlencode ahead of time, we'll do that here.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
function _make_signed_request( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $token, $token_secret, $signature_method, $url, $params = array() ) {

  // Only support GET in this function
  $method = 'GET';

  $signature_method = strtoupper( $signature_method );
  if( $signature_method != 'PLAINTEXT' && $signature_method != 'HMAC-SHA1' ) {
    print "Invalid signature method: ${signature_method}\n";
    return false;
  }

  $oauth_nonce = rand( 0, 999999 );
  $oauth_timestamp = time();
  $oauth_version = '1.0';

  $params['oauth_consumer_key'] = $consumer_key;
  $params['oauth_nonce'] = $oauth_nonce;
  $params['oauth_signature_method'] = $signature_method;
  $params['oauth_timestamp'] = $oauth_timestamp;
  $params['oauth_version'] = $oauth_version;

  if( $token ) {
    $params['oauth_token'] = $token;
  }
  if( ! $token_secret ) {
    $token_secret = '';
  }

  // Params need to be sorted by key
  ksort( $params, SORT_STRING );

  // Urlencode params and generate param string
  $param_list = array();
  foreach( $params as $key => $value ) {
    $param_list[] = urlencode( $key ) . '=' . urlencode( $value );
  }
  $param_string = join( '&', $param_list );

  // Generate base string (needed for SHA1)
  $base_string = urlencode( $method ) . '&' . urlencode( $url ) . '&' .
    urlencode( $param_string );

  // Generate secret
  $secret = urlencode( $consumer_secret ) . '&' . urlencode( $token_secret );
  if( $signature_method == 'PLAINTEXT' ) {
    $signature = $secret;
  } else if( $signature_method == 'HMAC-SHA1' ) {
    $signature = base64_encode( hash_hmac( 'sha1', $base_string, $secret, true ) );
  }

  // Append signature
  $param_string .= '&oauth_signature=' . urlencode( $signature );
  $final_url = $url . '?' . $param_string;

  // Make curl call
  $ch = curl_init();
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_URL, $final_url );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_AUTOREFERER, 1 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_RETURNTRANSFER, 1 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_FOLLOWLOCATION, 0 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_SSL_VERIFYPEER, 0 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_SSL_VERIFYHOST, 0 );

  $timeout = 2; // seconds
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_TIMEOUT, $timeout );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_CONNECTTIMEOUT, $timeout );

  $contents = curl_exec($ch);
  $ret_code = curl_getinfo( $ch, CURLINFO_HTTP_CODE );
  $errno = curl_errno($ch);
  $error_str = curl_error($ch);

  if( $errno || $error_str ) {
    //print "Error: ${error_str} (${errno})\n";
  }

  //print "Response code: ${ret_code}\n";
  //print "Contents:\n${contents}\n\n";

  curl_close($ch);

  $data = array(
    'return_code' => $ret_code,
    'contents'    => $contents,
    'error_str'   => $error_str,
    'errno'       => $errno
  );

  return $data;
}

///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//  FUNCTION oauth_response_to_array
/// @brief Break up the oauth response data into an associate array
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
function oauth_response_to_array( $response ) {
  $data = array();
  foreach( explode( '&', $response ) as $param ) {
    $parts = explode( '=', $param );
    if( count( $parts ) == 2 ) {
      $data[urldecode($parts[0])] = urldecode($parts[1]);
    }
  }
  return $data;
}

```

### Sample XML Response for Game API Request

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This XML snippet provides an example of the data returned by the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Game API when requesting information for a specific game, such as 'nfl'. It includes details like `game_key`, `game_id`, `name`, `code`, `type`, `url`, and `season`.

```XML
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<fantasy_content xml:lang="en-US" yahoo:uri="http://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/game/nfl" xmlns:yahoo="http://www.yahooapis.com/v1/base.rng" time="30.575037002563ms" copyright="Data provided by Yahoo! and STATS, LLC" xmlns="http://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/base.rng">
  <game>
    <game_key>257</game_key>
    <game_id>257</game_id>
    <name>Football</name>
    <code>nfl</code>
    <type>full</type>
    <url>https://football.fantasysports.yahoo.com/f1</url>
    <season>2011</season>
  </game>
</fantasy_content>

```

### Get OAuth 1.0a Request Token (PHP)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Retrieves an OAuth 1.0a request token from Yahoo's API. This is the initial step in the OAuth flow, preparing for user authorization. It uses a 'plaintext' signature method for simplicity in this example, and sets the callback to 'oob' (out-of-band) for console-based verification.

```php
function get_request_token( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret ) {

  $url = 'https://api.login.yahoo.com/oauth/v2/get_request_token';
  $signature_method = 'plaintext';

  $token = NULL;
  $token_secret = NULL;

  // Add in the lang pref and callback
  $xoauth_lang_pref = 'en-us';
  $oauth_callback = 'oob';  // Set OOB for ease of use -- could be a URL

  $params = array( 'xoauth_lang_pref' => $xoauth_lang_pref,
                   'oauth_callback'   => $oauth_callback );

  // Make the signed request without any token
  $response_data = _make_signed_request( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $token, $token_secret, $signature_method, $url, $params );

  if( $response_data && $response_data['return_code'] == 200 ) {

    $contents = $response_data['contents'];
    $data = oauth_response_to_array( $contents );

    //print_r( $data );

    return $data;
  }

  return false;
}
```

### Player API Overview and Operations

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Documents the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Player API, covering its purpose, supported HTTP operations (GET), URI formats for accessing player information and sub-resources, and the player key format. It also specifies the default sub-resource for player data.

```APIDOC
Player API:
  Description: With the Player API, you can obtain the player (athlete) related information, such as their name, professional team, and eligible positions. The player is identified in the context of a particular game, and can be requested as the base of your URI.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
  URIs:
    - https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/player/
    - https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/player//
    - https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/player/;out=,{sub_resource_2}
  Player key format:
    - .p.{player_id}
    - Example: pnfl.p.5479 or 223.p.5479
  Sub-resources:
    - Default sub-resource: metadata
```

--------------------------------

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API: Roster Resource Documentation

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Detailed documentation for the Roster resource in the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API, explaining its purpose, how players are organized into rosters, supported HTTP operations (GET, PUT), and various URI formats for accessing roster data by week or date.

```APIDOC
Roster Resource:
  Description:
    Players on a team are organized into rosters corresponding to certain weeks (NFL) or dates (MLB, NBA, NHL).
    Players can be in the starting lineup or on the bench.
    Only stats accumulated by players in the starting lineup are credited.
    API allows editing lineup by PUTting new positions for players.
    API allows adding/dropping players by POSTing new transactions to the league's transactions collection.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
    - PUT
  URIs:
    Base URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster
    Sub-resource URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster/
    NFL (specify week): https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster;week=10 (defaults to current roster)
    MLB/NHL/NBA (specify date): https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster;date=2011-05-01 (defaults to today's roster)
  Sub-resources:
    Default: players
```

### MLB/NBA/NHL Roster Update XML Payload Example

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

An XML payload example for updating player positions on an MLB, NBA, or NHL fantasy roster using the PUT API. Specifies coverage type as 'date' and includes player keys with their new positions.

```XML
<?xml version="1.0"?>
<fantasy_content>
  <roster>
    <coverage_type>date</coverage_type>
    <date>2011-05-01</date>

    <players>
      <player>
        <player_key>253.p.8332</player_key>
        <position>1B</position>
      </player>
      <player>
        <player_key>253.p.1423</player_key>
        <position>BN</position>
      </player>
    </players>
  </roster>
</fantasy_content>
```

### Transactions Collection API Overview

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Provides an overview of the Transactions API, detailing how to obtain information via GET from a collection of transactions simultaneously and how to perform operations like adding/dropping players or proposing trades via POST. Each element beneath the Transactions Collection will be a Transaction Resource.

```APIDOC
Transactions Collection:
  Description: API for obtaining transaction information and performing operations (add/drop players, propose trades).
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET: Retrieve transaction data from a collection.
    - POST: Perform operations like adding/dropping players or proposing trades.
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API: Roster Resource Documentation

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Comprehensive documentation for the Roster resource within the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. It outlines the resource's purpose, supported HTTP methods (GET, PUT), various URI patterns for accessing rosters by team, week, or date, and identifies default sub-resources.

```APIDOC
Roster resource:
  Description:
    Players on a team are organized into rosters corresponding to certain weeks (NFL) or dates (MLB, NBA, NHL).
    Each player on a roster will be assigned a position if theyre in the starting lineup, or will be on the bench.
    Only stats accumulated by players in your starting lineup are credited.
    API allows editing lineup by PUTting new positions for players on a roster.
    Adding/dropping players is done by POSTing new transactions to the leagues transactions collection.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
    - PUT
  URIs:
    Base URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster
    Sub-resource URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster/
    NFL (week parameter): https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster;week=10 (defaults to current roster)
    MLB, NHL, NBA (date parameter): https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster;date=2011-05-01 (defaults to todays roster)
  Sub-resources:
    Default: players
```

--------------------------------

### Reject a Pending Trade (PUT XML)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This XML example illustrates how to reject a pending trade proposed to your team. The `action` element is set to 'reject', and a `trade_note` can be provided to explain the rejection.

```XML
<?xml version='1.0'?>
<fantasy_content>
  <transaction>
    <transaction_key>248.l.55438.pt.11</transaction_key>
    <type>pending_trade</type>
    <action>reject</action>
    <trade_note>No way!</trade_note>
  </transaction>
</fantasy_content>
```

--------------------------------

### Transactions Collection API Overview

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Provides an overview of the Transactions API, enabling retrieval of transaction information via GET and performing operations like adding/dropping players or proposing trades via POST. Each element within the collection is a Transaction Resource.

```APIDOC
Description: Obtain information from a collection of transactions simultaneously via GET. POST to add/drop players or propose trades.
Supported HTTP Operations:
  - GET
  - POST
```

--------------------------------

### Retrieve Yahoo Fantasy Sports Game Data via HTTP GET

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Shows a direct HTTP GET request URL to access fantasy game information for a specific `game_code` (e.g., 'nfl') using the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API.

```HTTP
https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/game/nfl
```

### Example XML Response for Team Projected Points

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

An illustrative XML snippet demonstrating the structure for team projected points data, including coverage type (e.g., 'week'), the specific week number, and the total projected points. This fragment is typically part of a larger matchup or scoreboard response.

```xml
<team_projected_points>
  <coverage_type>week</coverage_type>
  <week>16</week>
  <total>127.28</total>
</team_projected_points>
```

```XML
          <image_url>https://l.yimg.com/a/i/us/sp/v/mlb/players_l/20110503x/7382.jpg?x=46&amp;y=60&amp;xc=1&amp;yc=1&amp;wc=164&amp;hc=215&amp;q=100&amp;sig=QNOFMSgR6NuPxUwDMUSM1w--</image_url>
          <is_undroppable>0</is_undroppable>
          <position_type>B</position_type>
          <eligible_positions>
            <position>3B</position>
            <position>Util</position>
            <position>DL</position>
          </eligible_positions>
          <has_player_notes>1</has_player_notes>
          <has_recent_player_notes>1</has_recent_player_notes>
          <selected_position>
            <coverage_type>date</coverage_type>
            <date>2011-07-22</date>
            <position>DL</position>
          </selected_position>
          <starting_status>
            <coverage_type>date</coverage_type>
            <date>2011-07-22</date>
            <is_starting>1</is_starting>
          </starting_status>
        </player>
      </players>
    </roster>
  </team>
</fantasy_content>
```

### Make Public Requests with PHP using 2-legged OAuth

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This PHP example demonstrates how to make public requests to the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API using 2-legged OAuth. It initializes an OAuth object with consumer key and secret, then attempts to fetch data from a public endpoint. Error handling for OAuth exceptions is included to catch potential issues during the fetch operation.

```php
<?php
$consumer_key = '<INSERT CONSUMER KEY HERE>';
$consumer_secret = '<INSERT CONSUMER SECRET HERE>';

$o = new OAuth( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret,
                OAUTH_SIG_METHOD_HMACSHA1,
                OAUTH_AUTH_TYPE_URI );

$url = 'https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/game/nfl';

try {
  if( $o->fetch( $url ) ) {

    print $o->getLastResponse();

    print "Successful fetch\n";
  } else {
    print "Couldn't fetch\n";
  }
} catch( OAuthException $e ) {
  print 'Error: ' . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
  print 'Response: ' . $e->lastResponse . "\n";

}
?>
```

--------------------------------

### Teams API Overview and Operations

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Documents the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Teams API, detailing its purpose, supported HTTP operations (GET), and various URI formats for accessing team collections and sub-resources. It explains how to retrieve information for teams within a league or owned by a specific user.

```APIDOC
Teams API:
  Description: With the Teams API, you can obtain information from a collection of teams simultaneously. The teams collection is qualified in the URI by a particular league to obtain information about teams within the league, or by a particular user (and optionally, a game) to obtain information about the teams owned by the user. Each element beneath the Teams Collection will be a Team Resource.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
  URIs:
    - /teams/{sub_resource}
    - /teams;team_keys={team_key1},{team_key2}/{sub_resource}
    - /teams;out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
    - /teams;team_keys={team_key1},{team_key2};out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
```

--------------------------------

### Disallow an Accepted Trade (PUT XML)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This XML example is used by league commissioners to disallow an accepted trade that is pending. The `action` element is set to 'disallow' for the given `transaction_key`.

```XML
<?xml version='1.0'?>
<fantasy_content>
  <transaction>
    <transaction_key>248.l.55438.pt.11</transaction_key>
    <type>pending_trade</type>
    <action>disallow</action>
  </transaction>
</fantasy_content>
```

### Leagues Collection API Reference

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

API documentation for the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Leagues collection, enabling simultaneous retrieval of information from multiple leagues. It outlines supported HTTP operations (GET) and various URI formats for accessing league sub-resources, including options for specifying multiple league keys or outputting multiple sub-resources.

```APIDOC
Leagues collection:
  Description: With the Leagues API, you can obtain information from a collection of leagues simultaneously. Each element beneath the Leagues Collection will be a League Resource.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
  URIs:
    - Any sub-resource valid for a league is a valid sub-resource under the leagues collection.
    - /leagues/{sub_resource}
    - /leagues;league_keys={league_key1},{league_key2}/{sub_resource}
    - Multiple sub-resources:
      - /leagues;out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
      - /leagues;league_keys={league_key1},{league_key2};out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
```

### Edit Waiver Claim Priority or FAAB Bid (PUT XML)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This XML example demonstrates how to use the `PUT` method to modify an existing waiver claim. It allows updating the `waiver_priority` and `faab_bid` for a specific transaction identified by its `transaction_key`.

```XML
<?xml version='1.0'?>
<fantasy_content>
  <transaction>
    <transaction_key>248.l.55438.w.c.2_6093</transaction_key>
    <type>waiver</type>
    <waiver_priority>1</waiver_priority>
    <faab_bid>20</faab_bid>
  </transaction>
</fantasy_content>
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Transaction API Overview and Supported Operations

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Provides an overview of the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Transaction API, detailing its purpose for retrieving and managing league transactions, including adds, drops, trades, and settings changes. It also lists the supported HTTP methods (GET, PUT, DELETE) for interacting with the API, enabling users to query, modify, and cancel transactions.

```APIDOC
Transaction API:
  Description: Obtain information about transactions (adds, drops, trades, and league settings changes) performed on a league.
  Operations:
    - GET
    - PUT
    - DELETE
```

### Yahoo Fantasy API Collection Filtering by Player Keys

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This example demonstrates how to filter a collection to retrieve specific players by their unique keys. By appending `player_keys` to the collection URL, you can narrow down the results to only the desired players. This is a common method for targeted data retrieval within larger collections.

```APIDOC
/fantasy/v2/;player_keys=,{player_key2}
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API: Get Team Details Endpoint

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

API endpoint to retrieve comprehensive details for a specific Yahoo Fantasy Sports team. This endpoint returns an XML response containing various team attributes and manager information.

```APIDOC
GET https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team/{team_key}

Parameters:
  team_key: string (Path Parameter) - The unique identifier for the fantasy team (e.g., 223.l.431.t.1).
```

--------------------------------

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Teams API

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Documents the Teams API for obtaining information about a collection of teams simultaneously. This API supports GET operations and allows for various URI structures to query teams by league, user, or specific team keys, and to extract multiple sub-resources.

```APIDOC
Teams API:
  Description: Obtain information from a collection of teams simultaneously. The collection can be qualified by a particular league or by a particular user (and optionally, a game).
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
  URIs:
    - /teams/{sub_resource}
    - /teams;team_keys={team_key1},{team_key2}/{sub_resource}
    - /teams;out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
    - /teams;team_keys={team_key1},{team_key2};out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
  Sub-resources: Any sub-resource valid for a team is a valid sub-resource under the teams collection.
```

--------------------------------

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Player API

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Documents the Player API for retrieving athlete-related information such as name, professional team, and eligible positions. This API supports GET operations and allows for various URI structures to query player data and extract multiple sub-resources.

```APIDOC
Player API:
  Description: Obtain player (athlete) related information, such as their name, professional team, and eligible positions. The player is identified in the context of a particular game.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
  URIs:
    - https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/player/
    - https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/player//
    - https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/player/;out=,{sub_resource_2}
  Player key format:
    - .p.{player_id}
    - Example: pnfl.p.5479 or 223.p.5479
  Sub-resources:
    - Default sub-resource: metadata
```

--------------------------------

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API: Roster Update PUT Method

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Documentation for the PUT method used to modify a team's roster in the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. It outlines the endpoint URL, the purpose of the operation (changing player positions or starting lineup status), and general rules for the update process.

```APIDOC
Method: PUT
Endpoint: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster
Purpose: Modify a subset of players on the roster for a particular day, specifically changing their position or whether theyre in the starting lineup.
Constraints:
  - You may move as many players as you like in your input XML.
  - Players whose position is not changed will stay in the same position they were previously.
  - Invalid moves will result in an error and no changes will be made.
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API: Get Team Matchups Endpoint

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

API endpoint to retrieve matchup details for a specific Yahoo Fantasy Sports team over specified weeks. The response includes detailed information about each matchup, including participating teams and their scores.

```APIDOC
GET https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team/{team_key}/matchups;weeks={weeks}

Parameters:
  team_key: string (Path Parameter) - The unique identifier for the fantasy team (e.g., 223.l.431.t.1).
  weeks: string (Query Parameter) - A comma-separated list of week numbers for which to retrieve matchups (e.g., 1,5).
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API - Users Collection Overview

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This section details the general HTTP operations supported by the API and provides a comprehensive overview of the Users collection. It describes its purpose, supported HTTP methods, and how sub-resources are handled, emphasizing its recommendation for login-related functionalities.

```APIDOC
General API Information:
  HTTP Operations Supported: GET
  URIs: It is generally recommended that you instead use the Users collection, passing along the `use_login` flag.
  Sub-resources: N/A (Default)

Users collection:
  Description: With the Users API, you can obtain information from a collection of users simultaneously. Each element beneath the Users Collection will be a User Resource.
  HTTP Operations Supported: GET
  Sub-resources: Any sub-resource valid for a user is a valid sub-resource under the users collection.
```

### Update Fantasy Roster Player Positions (PUT API)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Documents the PUT API endpoint for modifying player positions on a fantasy roster. It specifies the URL, input XML format, and behavior for invalid moves. This allows users to change player positions or starting lineup status.

```APIDOC
Method: PUT
URL: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//roster
Purpose: Modify a subset of players on the roster for a particular day, specifically in terms of changing their position or whether theyre in the starting lineup.
Input XML:
  - Players to be moved are specified by player_key and new position.
  - Any players whose position you do not change will stay in the same position they were previously.
Error Handling: If you try to move players in an invalid way, you will receive an error and no changes will be made.
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API Introduction and Overview

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This section introduces the Yahoo Fantasy Sports APIs, detailing their purpose for accessing fantasy sports data across various sports like Football, Baseball, Basketball, and Hockey. It explains the RESTful model, identifying resources (game, league, team, player) and collections, and how they form the building blocks of the API. It also touches upon the historical context of Yahoo's fantasy games and the merging of free and plus versions.

```APIDOC
The Fantasy Sports APIs provide URIs used to access fantasy sports data.
Currently the APIs support retrieval of Fantasy Football, Baseball, Basketball, and Hockey data including game, league, team, and player information. The APIs are based on a RESTful model. Therefore, resources like game, league, team, player etc. and collections like games, leagues, teams, players form the building blocks for these APIs. Each resource is identified by a resource ID, and a collection is identified by its scope, specified in the URI.

Historically, Yahoo! has provided two full draft and trade style fantasy football and baseball games  a free version, and a plus version (which contains more features and content). With the 2010 seasons, the Free and Plus versions of Football and Baseball have merged. Each game is comprised of many leagues, which typically contain 8-12 teams, which are managed by one or more users. At the beginning of a leagues season, professional athletes (players) are uniquely assigned or chosen through a draft to each team. The players that are not chosen or assigned are available to be acquired via a free-agent or waiver wire process (a transaction). These teams compete against each other based on statistics from real-world competitions based on categories like touchdowns, yards gained, batting average and ERA. Many fantasy sport rules can be set and changed within a league; for instance, the roster positions, statistics used to score, scoring modifiers, and game style are configurable.

The game structure means that a lot of fantasy data is relevant only in the context of a particular league and team. For instance, without the leagues scoring rules, the statistics compiled by a player in a real-life competition are not meaningful to a particular league. Three rushing touchdowns by a running back is irrelevant to a league that only considers defensive players. Many leagues are private  the information about them is only available to users that are a members.
```

--------------------------------

### Yahoo Fantasy API Collection Filtering by Logged-in User

This example demonstrates how to filter a collection to retrieve data specific to the currently logged-in user. By including the `use_login=1` parameter, the API will return results relevant to the authenticated user's context. This is useful for personalized data access within a collection.

```APIDOC
/fantasy/v2/;use_login=1
```

### PHP OAuth 1.0a Client Implementation

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This PHP script demonstrates a complete OAuth 1.0a client implementation from scratch. It includes a core helper function, `_make_signed_request`, which handles OAuth parameter generation, sorting, URL encoding, and signature creation (PLAINTEXT and HMAC-SHA1) for GET requests. It also provides a utility function, `oauth_response_to_array`, to parse OAuth responses into an associative array. The script utilizes cURL for making HTTP requests and includes configuration placeholders for consumer keys and secrets.

```php
<?php
// **** POTENTIAL CONFIGURATION STARTS HERE ****

// MODIFY: Insert your own consumer key and secret here!
$consumer_data = array();
$consumer_data['test']['key']    = '<INSERT CONSUMER KEY HERE>';
$consumer_data['test']['secret'] = '<INSERT CONSUMER SECRET HERE>';

// **** HELPER FUNCTIONS START HERE ****

///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//  FUNCTION _make_signed_request
/// @brief Helper function to make a signed OAuth request. Only allows GET
///        requests at the moment. Will add on standard OAuth params, but
///        you may need to fill in non-generic ones ahead of time.
///
/// @param[in]  $consumer_key      Application consumer key
/// @param[in]  $consumer_secret   Application consumer secret
/// @param[in]  $token             Token (request or access token)
/// @param[in]  $token_secret      Token secret
/// @param[in]  $signature_method  'PLAINTEXT' or 'HMAC-SHA1'
/// @param[in]  $url               URL to make request to
/// @param[in]  $params            Array of key=>val for params. Don't
///                                urlencode ahead of time, we'll do that here.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
function _make_signed_request( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $token, $token_secret, $signature_method, $url, $params = array() ) {

  // Only support GET in this function
  $method = 'GET';

  $signature_method = strtoupper( $signature_method );
  if( $signature_method != 'PLAINTEXT' && $signature_method != 'HMAC-SHA1' ) {
    print "Invalid signature method: ${signature_method}\n";
    return false;
  }

  $oauth_nonce = rand( 0, 999999 );
  $oauth_timestamp = time();
  $oauth_version = '1.0';

  $params['oauth_consumer_key'] = $consumer_key;
  $params['oauth_nonce'] = $oauth_nonce;
  $params['oauth_signature_method'] = $signature_method;
  $params['oauth_timestamp'] = $oauth_timestamp;
  $params['oauth_version'] = $oauth_version;

  if( $token ) {
    $params['oauth_token'] = $token;
  }
  if( ! $token_secret ) {
    $token_secret = '';
  }

  // Params need to be sorted by key
  ksort( $params, SORT_STRING );

  // Urlencode params and generate param string
  $param_list = array();
  foreach( $params as $key => $value ) {
    $param_list[] = urlencode( $key ) . '=' . urlencode( $value );
  }
  $param_string = join( '&', $param_list );

  // Generate base string (needed for SHA1)
  $base_string = urlencode( $method ) . '&' . urlencode( $url ) . '&' .
    urlencode( $param_string );

  // Generate secret
  $secret = urlencode( $consumer_secret ) . '&' . urlencode( $token_secret );
  if( $signature_method == 'PLAINTEXT' ) {
    $signature = $secret;
  } else if( $signature_method == 'HMAC-SHA1' ) {
    $signature = base64_encode( hash_hmac( 'sha1', $base_string, $secret, true ) );
  }

  // Append signature
  $param_string .= '&oauth_signature=' . urlencode( $signature );
  $final_url = $url . '?' . $param_string;

  // Make curl call
  $ch = curl_init();
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_URL, $final_url );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_AUTOREFERER, 1 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_RETURNTRANSFER, 1 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_FOLLOWLOCATION, 0 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_SSL_VERIFYPEER, 0 );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_SSL_VERIFYHOST, 0 );

  $timeout = 2; // seconds
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_TIMEOUT, $timeout );
  curl_setopt( $ch, CURLOPT_CONNECTTIMEOUT, $timeout );

  $contents = curl_exec($ch);
  $ret_code = curl_getinfo( $ch, CURLINFO_HTTP_CODE );
  $errno = curl_errno($ch);
  $error_str = curl_error($ch);

  if( $errno || $error_str ) {
    //print "Error: ${error_str} (${errno})\n";
  }

  //print "Response code: ${ret_code}\n";
  //print "Contents:\n${contents}\n\n";

  curl_close($ch);

  $data = array(
    'return_code' => $ret_code,
    'contents'    => $contents,
    'error_str'   => $error_str,
    'errno'       => $errno
  );

  return $data;
}

///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//  FUNCTION oauth_response_to_array
/// @brief Break up the oauth response data into an associate array
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
function oauth_response_to_array( $response ) {
  $data = array();
  foreach( explode( '&', $response ) as $param ) {
    $parts = explode( '=', $param );
    if( count( $parts ) == 2 ) {
      $data[urldecode($parts[0])] = urldecode($parts[1]);
    }
  }
  return $data;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Make Public Requests with PHP OAuth

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Demonstrates how to perform public data requests to the Yahoo Fantasy API using 2-legged OAuth in PHP. This method utilizes only the consumer key and secret, bypassing the need for an access token, suitable for accessing non-user-specific data. The example shows fetching game data and handling potential OAuth exceptions.

```PHP
<?php
$consumer_key = '<INSERT CONSUMER KEY HERE>';
$consumer_secret = '<INSERT CONSUMER SECRET HERE>';

$o = new OAuth( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret,
                OAUTH_SIG_METHOD_HMACSHA1,
                OAUTH_AUTH_TYPE_URI );

$url = 'https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/game/nfl';

try {
  if( $o->fetch( $url ) ) {

    print $o->getLastResponse();

    print "Successful fetch\n";
  } else {
    print "Couldn't fetch\n";
  }
} catch( OAuthException $e ) {
  print 'Error: ' . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
  print 'Response: ' . $e->lastResponse . "\n";

}
?>
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports API: League Resource Overview

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Provides an overview of the League API, including its purpose, supported HTTP operations, URI structure, league key format, and default sub-resources for retrieving league-related information. It clarifies how leagues are organized within the Fantasy Sports ecosystem.

```APIDOC
League Resource:
  Description: When users join a Fantasy Football, Baseball, Basketball, or Hockey draft and trade game, they are organized into leagues with a limited number of friends or other Yahoo! users, with each user managing a Team. With the League API, you can obtain the league related information, like the league name, the number of teams, the draft status, et cetera. Leagues only exist in the context of a particular Game, although you can request a League Resource as the base of your URI by using the global. A particular user can only retrieve data for private leagues of which they are a member, or for public leagues.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
  URIs:
    Base URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/league/
    Sub-resource URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/league//
    Multiple Sub-resources URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/league/;out=,{sub_resource_2}
  League Key Format:
    Format: .l.{league_id}
    Example: pnfl.l.431 or 223.l.431
    Note: The separator between the game_key and league_id is a lower case L (not the number 1).
  Sub-resources:
    Default: metadata
```

### PHP OAuth Client for Yahoo Fantasy Sports API

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This PHP script demonstrates a basic OAuth client for the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. It attempts to load existing access tokens from a file, refreshes them if expired or unauthorized, and then makes an API call to retrieve NFL team data. Users must configure their consumer key and secret and have the PHP OAuth extension installed.

```PHP
<?php
// **** POTENTIAL CONFIGURATION STARTS HERE ****

// NOTE: If you don't have the OAuth extension hooked into PHP, you may need
//  to include it here.

// MODIFY: Insert whichever URL you'd like to try below. By default, the
//  following URL will try to pull out the NFL teams for the logged-in user
$url = 'https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/users;use_login=1/games;game_keys=nfl/teams';
$scope = 'test';

// MODIFY: Insert your own consumer key and secret here!
$consumer_data = array();
$consumer_data['test']['key'] = '<INSERT CONSUMER KEY HERE>';
$consumer_data['test']['secret'] = '<INSERT CONSUMER SECRET HERE>';

// **** MAIN PROGRAM START HERE ****

$consumer_key = $consumer_data[$scope]['key'];
$consumer_secret = $consumer_data[$scope]['secret'];

// By default, try to store token information in /tmp folder
$token_file_name = '/tmp/oauth_data_token_storage_' . $consumer_key . '.out';

$access_token = NULL;
$access_secret = NULL;
$access_session = NULL;
$access_verifier = NULL;
$store_access_token_data = false;

if( file_exists( $token_file_name ) &&
    $tok_fh = fopen( $token_file_name, 'r' ) ) {

  $invalid_file = false;

  // Get first line: access token
  $access_token = fgets( $tok_fh );
  if( $access_token ) {
    // Get next line: access secret
    $access_secret = fgets( $tok_fh );
    if( $access_secret ) {
      // Get next line: access session handle
      $access_session = fgets( $tok_fh );
      if( ! $access_session ) {
        $invalid_file = true;
      }
    } else {
      $invalid_file = true;
    }
  } else {
    $invalid_file = true;
  }

  if( $invalid_file ) {
    print "File did not seem to be formatted correctly -- needs 3 lines with access token, secret, and session handle.\n";
    $access_token = NULL;
    $access_secret = NULL;
    $access_session = NULL;
  } else {
    print "Got access token information!\n";

    $access_token = rtrim( $access_token );
    $access_secret = rtrim( $access_secret );
    $access_session = rtrim( $access_session );

    print " Token: ${access_token}\n";
    print " Secret: ${access_secret}\n";
    print " Session Handle: ${access_session}\n\n";
  }

  // Done with file, close it up
  fclose( $tok_fh );

} else {
  print "Couldn't open ${token_file_name}, assuming we need to get a new request token.\n";
}

// 1. See if we have a stored access token/secret/session. If so, try to use
//    that token.
if( $access_token ) {

  $o = new OAuth( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret,
                  OAUTH_SIG_METHOD_HMACSHA1, OAUTH_AUTH_TYPE_URI );
  $o->enableDebug();

  $auth_failure = false;

  // Try to make request using stored token
  try {
    $o->setToken( $access_token, $access_secret );
    if( $o->fetch( $url ) ) {
      print "Got data from API:\n\n";
      print $o->getLastResponse() . "\n\n";

      print "Successful!\n";
      exit;
    } else {
      print "Couldn't fetch\n";
    }
  } catch( OAuthException $e ) {
    print 'Error: ' . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
    print 'Error Code: ' . $e->getCode() . "\n";
    print 'Response: ' . $e->lastResponse . "\n";

    if( $e->getCode() == 401 ) {
      $auth_failure = true;
    }
  }

  // 2. If we get an auth error, try to refresh the token using the session.
  if( $auth_failure ) {

    try {
      $response = $o->getAccessToken( 'https://api.login.yahoo.com/oauth/v2/get_token', $access_session, $access_verifier );
    } catch( OAuthException $e ) {
      print 'Error: ' . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
      print 'Response: ' . $e->lastResponse . "\n";

      $response = NULL;
    }

    print_r( $response );

    if( $response ) {
      $access_token = $response['oauth_token'];
      $access_secret = $response['oauth_token_secret'];
      $access_session = $response['oauth_session_handle'];
      $store_access_token_data = true;

      print "Was able to refresh access token:\n";
      print " Token: ${access_token}\n";
      print " Secret: ${access_secret}\n";
      print " Session Handle: ${access_session}\n\n";

    } else {

      $access_token = NULL;
      $access_secret = NULL;
      $access_session = NULL;
      print "Unable to refresh access token, will need to request a new one.\n";
    }
  }
}
```

--------------------------------

### Team Resource API Reference

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

API documentation for the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Team resource, providing details on how to retrieve team-specific information such as name, managers, logos, stats, and rosters for particular weeks. It specifies supported HTTP operations (GET), various URI patterns for accessing sub-resources, and the format for team keys. Access is restricted to members of private leagues or public leagues.

```APIDOC
Team resource:
  Description: The Team APIs allow you to retrieve information about a team within our fantasy games. The team is the basic unit for keeping track of a roster of players, and can be managed by either one or two managers (the second manager being called a co-manager). With the Team APIs, you can obtain team-related information, like the team name, managers, logos, stats and points, and rosters for particular weeks. Teams only exist in the context of a particular League, although you can request a Team Resource as the base of your URI by using the global. A particular user can only retrieve data about a team if that team is part of a private league of which the user is a member, or if its in a public league.
  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
  URIs:
    - https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team/
    - Sub-resource: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team//
    - Multiple sub-resources: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/team/;out=,{sub_resource_2}
  Team key format:
    - .l.{league_id}.t.{team_id}
    - Example: pnfl.l.431.t.1 or 223.l.431.t.1
  Sub-resources:
    - Default sub-resource: metadata
```

--------------------------------

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Transaction Key Formats

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Details the various formats for transaction keys used in the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API, which are crucial for uniquely identifying specific transactions within a league. It provides distinct key structures and examples for completed transactions, active waiver claims, and pending trades, ensuring accurate targeting of API requests.

```APIDOC
Transaction Key Formats:
  Completed transactions: .l.{league_id}.tr.{transaction_id}
    Example: pnfl.l.431.tr.26 or 223.l.431.tr.26
  Waiver claims: .l.{league_id}.w.c.{claim_id}
    Example: 257.l.193.w.c.2_6390
  Pending trades: .l.{league_id}.pt.{pending_trade_id}
    Example: 257.l.193.pt.1
```

### XML for Pending Trade Transaction in Yahoo Fantasy Sports API

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This XML snippet demonstrates a proposed pending trade transaction in the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. It includes details such as the trader and tradee team keys, the proposed time, a trade note, and the players involved in the trade (though the player list is truncated in this example).

```XML
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<fantasy_content xmlns:yahoo="http://www.yahooapis.com/v1/base.rng" xmlns="http://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/base.rng" xml:lang="en-US" yahoo:uri="http://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/transaction/257.l.193.pt.1" time="45.558929443359ms" copyright="Data provided by Yahoo! and STATS, LLC">
  <transaction>
    <transaction_key>257.l.193.pt.1</transaction_key>
    <type>pending_trade</type>
    <status>proposed</status>
    <trader_team_key>257.l.193.t.2</trader_team_key>
    <tradee_team_key>257.l.193.t.1</tradee_team_key>
    <trade_proposed_time>1310694832</trade_proposed_time>
    <trade_note>This is a great trade, fo' shizzle.</trade_note>
    <players count="2">
      <player>
        <player_key>257.p.8261</player_key>
        <player_id>8261</player_id>
        <name>
          <full>Adrian Peterson</full>
          <first>Adrian</first>

```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports User Resource API Overview

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Documentation for the User API, detailing its purpose for retrieving fantasy information for a Yahoo! user. It outlines capabilities and important usage notes.

```APIDOC
User resource:
  Description: Retrieve fantasy information for a particular Yahoo! user.
  Capabilities:
    - View games a user is playing.
    - View leagues a user belongs to.
    - View teams owned within those games.
  Usage Notes:
    - Currently only viewable for the logged-in user.
    - Recommended approach: Use the 'Users collection' with the 'use_login' flag instead of trying to request a User resource directly from its URI.
```

```XML
</fantasy_content>
```

### Get OAuth 1.0a Request Token (PHP)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This function initiates the OAuth 1.0a flow by obtaining a temporary request token from Yahoo's OAuth endpoint. It uses plaintext signing for the initial request and sets a callback URL to 'oob' (out-of-band) for desktop applications, allowing the user to manually enter the verifier. It relies on an external `_make_signed_request` function for the underlying OAuth signing and request execution, and `oauth_response_to_array` for parsing the response.

```php
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
//  FUNCTION get_request_token
/// @brief Get a request token for a given application.
///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////
function get_request_token( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret ) {

  $url = 'https://api.login.yahoo.com/oauth/v2/get_request_token';
  $signature_method = 'plaintext';

  $token = NULL;
  $token_secret = NULL;

  // Add in the lang pref and callback
  $xoauth_lang_pref = 'en-us';
  $oauth_callback = 'oob';  // Set OOB for ease of use -- could be a URL

  $params = array( 'xoauth_lang_pref' => $xoauth_lang_pref,
                   'oauth_callback'   => $oauth_callback );

  // Make the signed request without any token
  $response_data = _make_signed_request( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret, $token, $token_secret, $signature_method, $url, $params );

  if( $response_data && $response_data['return_code'] == 200 ) {

    $contents = $response_data['contents'];
    $data = oauth_response_to_array( $contents );

    //print_r( $data );

    return $data;
  }

  return false;
}
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Player XML Object Schema

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Defines the hierarchical structure and data types for a single player object as typically returned in XML format by the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. This schema includes core player identifiers, name components, team affiliations, various positional eligibilities, and status indicators like 'undroppable' or 'starting'.

```APIDOC
Player:
  player_key: string (e.g., "253.p.7746")
  player_id: integer (e.g., 7746)
  name:
    full: string (e.g., "Dustin Pedroia")
    first: string (e.g., "Dustin")
    last: string (e.g., "Pedroia")
    ascii_first: string (e.g., "Dustin")
    ascii_last: string (e.g., "Pedroia")
  editorial_player_key: string (e.g., "mlb.p.7746")
  editorial_team_key: string (e.g., "mlb.t.2")
  editorial_team_full_name: string (e.g., "Boston Red Sox")
  editorial_team_abbr: string (e.g., "Bos")
  uniform_number: integer (e.g., 15)
  display_position: string (e.g., "2B")
  image_url: string (URL)
  is_undroppable: integer (0 or 1)
  position_type: string (e.g., "B")
  eligible_positions: array of string
    position: string (e.g., "1B", "2B", "OF", "Util")
  has_player_notes: integer (0 or 1)
  has_recent_player_notes: integer (0 or 1) (Optional)
  selected_position:
    coverage_type: string (e.g., "date")
    date: string (YYYY-MM-DD)
    position: string (e.g., "2B")
  starting_status:
    coverage_type: string (e.g., "date")
    date: string (YYYY-MM-DD)
    is_starting: integer (0 or 1)
```

### Understanding Sub-Resources in Yahoo Fantasy API

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Explains the core concept of sub-resources within the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API, detailing how resources and collections can be nested within parent resources. It covers the distinction between singular resource sub-resources and collection sub-resources, how their scope is defined by the parent, and introduces the `out` parameter for fetching additional, non-chained sub-resources.

```APIDOC
Sub-Resources:
  - Definition: Resources and Collections that can live within the scope of a parent Resource.
  - Scope: Typically defined by the parent Resource (e.g., Players Collection as sub-resource of a League).
  - Collection as sub-resource: Used when multiple instances of a Resource can be contained within another (e.g., Teams Collection within a League).
  - Singular Resource as sub-resource: Used when only one instance of a Resource makes sense within another.
  - Chaining: Directly specified by the URI, allowing sequential access to nested resources.
  - `out` parameter:
    - Purpose: Allows specifying one level of extra sub-resources to pull in, outside the main resource chain.
    - Limitation: Cannot pass parameters to `out` sub-resources, and chaining other resources off them is generally not supported.
```

--------------------------------

### General API HTTP Operations and URI Recommendation

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

### General URI Structure for Applying Parameters

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This snippet illustrates the general URI structure for applying semicolon-delimited key-value parameters to resources and collections within the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. Parameters are placed after the resource or collection name, allowing for filtering and customization of data retrieval.

```APIDOC
/fantasy/v2/{resource}/{resource_key};{key}={value};{key}={value}/{collection};{key}={value};{key}={value}/{collection};{key}={value}/{resource};{key}={value}
```

--------------------------------

### Applying Parameters in Yahoo Fantasy API URIs

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Describes how parameters are applied to resources and collections in the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. Parameters are semicolon-delimited key-value pairs placed after the resource or collection name in the URI. It clarifies that resource keys, `out` parameters, and other filters are specific types of parameters.

```APIDOC
Parameters:
  - Format: Semicolon-delimited key-value pairs.
  - Placement: After the Resource or Collection name in the URI.
  - Entry-point Resources (e.g., Game, League, Team, Player): Parameters belong after the `resource_key`.
  - Types: Resource keys, `out` parameters, and other filters are specific types of parameters.
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Game API Reference

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This section outlines the core structure and usage of the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Game API. It details supported HTTP operations, URI patterns for accessing game resources and sub-resources, and the format of `game_key` parameters, including how `game_code` is translated to `game_id`.

```APIDOC
Game API:
  HTTP Operations Supported: GET
  URIs:
    Base URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/game/
    Sub-resource URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/game/<game_key>/<sub_resource>
    Multiple Sub-resources URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/game/<game_key>;out=<sub_resource_1>,<sub_resource_2>
  Game Key Format: {game_code} or {game_id} (Example: 'pnfl' or '223')
    Note: If game_code is specified, it will be translated to the corresponding game_id in the response XML.
  Default Sub-resource: metadata
```

--------------------------------

### Fantasy Sports API Overview and Resource Types

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Describes the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API, its RESTful nature, supported sports (Football, Baseball, Basketball, Hockey), and the core resources available such as game, league, team, player, and transaction. It explains how these resources form the building blocks of the API.

```APIDOC
Fantasy Sports API:
  Description: RESTful API for accessing fantasy sports data.
  Supported Sports: Football, Baseball, Basketball, Hockey
  Core Resources:
    - Game: Represents a fantasy sports game (e.g., Football, Baseball).
    - League: A collection of teams within a specific game, typically 8-12 teams.
    - Team: Managed by one or more users, part of a league.
    - Player: Professional athletes assigned to teams or available via transactions.
    - Transaction: Process for acquiring players (free-agent, waiver wire).
    - User: Manages teams.
  API Model: RESTful
  Resource Identification:
    - Individual Resources: Identified by a resource ID.
    - Collections: Identified by their scope in the URI.
  Contextual Data: Many data points (e.g., player statistics) are meaningful only within the context of a specific league's rules.
  Privacy: Many leagues are private; information is only available to members.
```

--------------------------------

### Using the 'out' Parameter for Extra Sub-Resources

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Illustrates how to use the `out` parameter to fetch additional sub-resources, like league settings, alongside specific teams within a league, in the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API.

```APIDOC
/fantasy/v2//;out=settings/;team_keys=,{team_key2}
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports User Resource API Overview

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Documentation for the Yahoo Fantasy Sports User API, which allows retrieval of fantasy information for a particular Yahoo! user. This includes games played, leagues joined, and teams owned within those games. It is primarily intended for accessing information about the logged-in user, typically via the Users collection with the `use_login` flag.

```APIDOC
User resource:
  Description:
    - Retrieve fantasy information for a particular Yahoo! user.
    - Information includes games played, leagues belonged to, and teams owned.
    - Primarily used for the logged-in user.
    - Recommended access: Use the 'Users collection' with the 'use_login' flag instead of direct URI requests.
  Related Actions (mentioned):
    - Edit waiver priority or FAAB bid (PUT /transaction/editwaiver)
    - Accept trade (PUT /transaction/accepttrade)
    - Reject trade (PUT /transaction/rejecttrade)
    - Allow/Disallow trade (PUT /transaction/allowtrade)
    - Vote against trade (PUT /transaction/voteagainst)
    - Cancel trade (DELETE /transaction)
```

--------------------------------

### Users Collection API Reference

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Provides detailed documentation for the Users API, enabling simultaneous retrieval of information for multiple users. It specifies supported HTTP methods and various URI patterns for extracting sub-resources and specific fields.

```APIDOC
Users Collection API:
  Description: Retrieve information for multiple users simultaneously. Each element is a User Resource.
  HTTP Methods:
    - GET
  URIs:
    - Base URI: /users;use_login=1
    - Sub-resource extraction: /users;use_login=1/{sub_resource}
    - Multiple sub-resources: /users;use_login=1;out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
    - Field selection: /users;field={field_name1},{field_name2}
    - Valid Sub-resources: Any sub-resource valid for a single User Resource.
```

--------------------------------

### PHP OAuth Request and Access Token Acquisition for Yahoo API

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

This PHP snippet demonstrates the full OAuth 1.0a flow to obtain a request token and then exchange it for an access token from Yahoo's API. It handles user interaction for the verifier code and includes error handling for token acquisition steps.

```php
if( ! $access_token ) {

  print "Better try to get a new access token.\n";
  $o = new OAuth( $consumer_key, $consumer_secret,
                  OAUTH_SIG_METHOD_HMACSHA1, OAUTH_AUTH_TYPE_URI );
  $o->enableDebug();

  $request_token = NULL;

  try {
    $response = $o->getRequestToken( "https://api.login.yahoo.com/oauth/v2/get_request_token", 'oob' );
    $request_token = $response['oauth_token'];
    $request_secret = $response['oauth_token_secret'];

    print "Hey! Go to this URL and tell us the verifier you get at the end.\n";
    print ' ' . $response['xoauth_request_auth_url'] . "\n";

  } catch( OAuthException $e ) {
    print $e->getMessage() . "\n";
  }

  // Wait for input, then try to use it to get a new access token.
  if( $request_token && $request_secret ) {
    print "Type the verifier and hit enter...\n";
    $verifier = fgets( STDIN );
    $verifier = rtrim( $verifier );

    print "Here's the verifier you gave us: ${verifier}\n";

    try {
      $o->setToken( $request_token, $request_secret );
      $response = $o->getAccessToken( 'https://api.login.yahoo.com/oauth/v2/get_token', NULL, $verifier );

      print "Got it!\n";
      $access_token = $response['oauth_token'];
      $access_secret = $response['oauth_token_secret'];
      $access_session = $response['oauth_session_handle'];
      $store_access_token_data = true;
      print " Token: ${access_token}\n";
      print " Secret: ${access_secret}\n";
      print " Session Handle: ${access_session}\n\n";

    } catch( OAuthException $e ) {
      print 'Error: ' . $e->getMessage() . "\n";
      print 'Response: ' . $e->lastResponse . "\n";
      print "Shoot, couldn't get the access token. :(\n";
    }
  }

}
```

--------------------------------

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Players Collection API Documentation

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Detailed documentation for the Players collection API, allowing retrieval of player information. It covers supported HTTP operations, URI structures for accessing player data and sub-resources, and various filtering options to narrow down player searches.

```APIDOC
Players collection

Description:
  With the Players API, you can obtain information from a collection of players simultaneously. To obtains general players information, the players collection can be qualified in the URI by a particular game, league or team. To obtain specific league or team related information, the players collection is qualified by the relevant league or team. Each element beneath the Players Collection will be a Player Resource.

HTTP Operations Supported:
  GET

URIs:
  Any sub-resource valid for a player is a valid sub-resource under the players collection.
  Any sub-resource for a collection of players is extracted using a URI like:
    /players/{sub_resource}
  OR
    /players;player_keys={player_key1},{player_key2}/{sub_resource}
  Multiple sub-resources can be extracted from players in the same URI using a format like:
    /players;out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}
  OR
    /players;player_keys={player_key1},{player_key2};out={sub_resource_1},{sub_resource_2}

Filters:
  The players collection can have filters such as the following to obtain a subset of a players collection that satisfy the filtering condition. The filters can be combined to obtain a more restricted list of players.

  Parameter | Values | Usage
  ----------|--------|------
  position  | Valid player positions | /players;position=QB (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  status    | A (all available players), FA (free agents only), W (waivers only), T (all taken players), K (keepers only) | /players;status=A (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  search    | player name | /players;search=smith (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  sort      | {stat_id}, NAME (last, first), OR (overall rank), AR (actual rank), PTS (fantasy points) | /players;sort=60 (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  sort_type | season, date (baseball, basketball, and hockey only), week (football only), lastweek (baseball, basketball, and hockey only), lastmonth | /players;sort_type=season (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  sort_season | year | /players;sort_type=season;sort_season=2010 (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  sort_date (baseball, basketball, and hockey only) | YYYY-MM-DD | /players;sort_type=date;sort_date=2010-02-01 (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  sort_week (football only) | week | /players;sort_type=week;sort_week=10 (Note: Applied only in a leagues context)
  start     | Any integer 0 or greater | /players;start=25
  count     | Any integer greater than 0 | /players;count=5
```

--------------------------------

### Sample XML Response for Team Matchups

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

This XML snippet demonstrates the response structure for retrieving a team's matchups for specified weeks from the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. It extends the basic team information with a 'matchups' section, detailing individual matchups, including week, status, winner, and participating teams with their points and projected points.

### Add/Drop Players or Propose Trades (POST)

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Explains how to use the POST HTTP method to add or drop players from a team, or to propose trades. Specifies the URI for POSTing to the transactions collection, which is `https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/league//transactions`.

```APIDOC
POST https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/league//transactions
  Description: Allows adding/dropping players or proposing trades.
  Usage: Used to modify team rosters or initiate trade proposals.
```

### XML for Completed Add/Drop Transaction

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Demonstrates the XML structure for a successful add/drop transaction, detailing the players involved, their transaction data (add/drop type, source, destination), and associated team keys.

```XML
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<fantasy_content xmlns:yahoo="http://www.yahooapis.com/v1/base.rng" xmlns="http://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/base.rng" xml:lang="en-US" yahoo:uri="http://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/transaction/257.l.193.tr.2" time="51.784038543701ms" copyright="Data provided by Yahoo! and STATS, LLC">
  <transaction>
    <transaction_key>257.l.193.tr.2</transaction_key>
    <transaction_id>2</transaction_id>
    <type>add/drop</type>
    <status>successful</status>
    <timestamp>1310694660</timestamp>
    <players count="2">
      <player>
        <player_key>257.p.7847</player_key>
        <player_id>7847</player_id>
        <name>
          <full>Owen Daniels</full>
          <first>Owen</first>
          <last>Daniels</last>
          <ascii_first>Owen</ascii_first>
          <ascii_last>Daniels</ascii_last>
        </name>
        <transaction_data>
          <type>add</type>
          <source_type>freeagents</source_type>
          <destination_type>team</destination_type>
          <destination_team_key>257.l.193.t.1</destination_team_key>
        </transaction_data>
      </player>
      <player>
        <player_key>257.p.6390</player_key>
        <player_id>6390</player_id>
        <name>
          <full>Anquan Boldin</full>
          <first>Anquan</first>
          <last>Boldin</last>
          <ascii_first>Anquan</ascii_first>
          <ascii_last>Boldin</ascii_last>
        </name>
        <transaction_data>
          <type>drop</type>
          <source_type>team</source_type>
          <source_team_key>257.l.193.t.1</source_team_key>
          <destination_type>waivers</destination_type>
        </transaction_data>
      </player>
    </players>
  </transaction>
</fantasy_content>
```

### Yahoo Fantasy Sports Transaction API Reference

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/index

Detailed API documentation for the Yahoo Fantasy Sports Transaction API, covering its purpose, supported HTTP methods, URI structures for accessing transaction resources, and specific key formats for different transaction types like completed transactions, waiver claims, and pending trades. It also lists default sub-resources.

```APIDOC
Transaction API:
  Description: Obtain information about transactions (adds, drops, trades, and league settings changes) performed on a league. Perform operations like editing waiver priorities or FAAB bids, modifying the state of pending trades, or canceling pending transactions.

  HTTP Operations Supported:
    - GET
    - PUT
    - DELETE

  URIs:
    - Base URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/transaction/
    - Sub-resource URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/transaction/<transaction_key>/<sub_resource>
    - Multiple Sub-resources URI: https://fantasysports.yahooapis.com/fantasy/v2/transaction/<transaction_key>;out=<sub_resource_1>,<sub_resource_2>

  Transaction Key Formats:
    - Completed transactions: .l.{league_id}.tr.{transaction_id}
      Example: pnfl.l.431.tr.26 or 223.l.431.tr.26
    - Waiver claims: .l.{league_id}.w.c.{claim_id}
      Example: 257.l.193.w.c.2_6390
    - Pending trades: .l.{league_id}.pt.{pending_trade_id}
      Example: 257.l.193.pt.1

  Sub-resources:
    - Default: metadata, players
```

--------------------------------

### General URI Structure for Parameters in Yahoo Fantasy API

Source: https://developer.yahoo.com/fantasysports/guide

Defines the general URI format for applying semicolon-delimited key-value parameters to resources and collections in the Yahoo Fantasy Sports API. Parameters are placed after the resource or collection name.

```APIDOC
/fantasy/v2/{resource}/{resource_key};{key}={value};{key}={value}/{collection};{key}={value};{key}={value}/{collection};{key}={value}/{resource};{key}={value}
```
